Yesterday's Groundbreaking Ceremony for the Engineering Hall at Jiaotong University 87

Chinese and Foreign Guests Attended Amidst Heavy Snow

Since Sun Ke and Li Zhaohuan successively became presidents of Jiaotong University in this city, they have been eager to expand the campus buildings and have established five-year and ten-year plans. In the past two years, the Zhixin West Building and the Iron and Wood Factory have been completed. Recently, the construction of an Engineering Hall has begun, and ground was broken on December 14th of last year. On the 20th of the same month, a groundbreaking ceremony was held, and the original metal and woodworking factories were dismantled to prepare the site. Details have been reported in this newspaper. It is now reported that the dismantling work has been completed, and yesterday a groundbreaking ceremony for the hall was held. President Li Zhaohuan of the university telegraphed Sun Ke, Minister of Railways, to come to Shanghai, and also invited prominent Chinese and foreign figures in Shanghai to participate. On that day, snow fell heavily and the weather was very cold, but the participants were still very enthusiastic. Among the guests were Japanese Chargé d'Affaires Shigemitsu Aoi, French Vice-Consul Han Shi Li, Shanghai Electric Power Company Chief Engineer E.I. Ed at, Jardine Engineering Corporation representative He Jin'en, U.S. Steel Corporation representative Bao Qisi, Swiss Sulzer Company representative Max Ted, and dozens of others. The ceremony began at 10:30 a.m. After the meeting, Li Zhaohuan gave a report, followed by a speech by Sun Ke. After the ceremony, the group braved the snow to lay the foundation stone at the site and took photographs before dispersing. The speeches of Li and Sun are recorded separately below.

President Li's Report Minister, Distinguished Guests, Today is the groundbreaking ceremony for the Engineering Hall of Jiaotong University. Because it is snowing today, it is inconvenient to hold the ceremony outside, so we have temporarily borrowed this classroom. We are very grateful and honored to have the Minister's instructions and the guidance of Chinese and foreign guests. Jiaotong University has a history of thirty-five years. After several reforms in the past, it has achieved its current situation. However, in the past ten years, various construction projects at the school have been stalled due to financial difficulties. Until the year before last, Minister Sun took office as the president of our school and set a five-year and ten-year plan for the entire construction of Jiaotong University. On the one hand, he boosted the spirit of Jiaotong University spiritually, and on the other hand, he rebuilt it materially. According to this plan, the new dormitory (Zhixin West Building) was completed last year. The second step was to build this factory, and the third step is the Engineering Hall. Construction began on December 14th last year, and the groundbreaking ceremony was held on the 20th. The estimated cost is 241,900 taels, excluding electrical equipment and other installations, totaling 500,000 yuan. It was originally scheduled to be completed in August of this year. However, because the snowfall this year is more severe than in previous years, the project cannot be completed according to the budget, or it may be completed in early September. Taking this opportunity, our school plans to hold a 35th-anniversary celebration in October or December, and the opening ceremony of the Engineering Hall will also be held at the same time. We also plan to hold an industrial exhibition. We hope that all guests will come to the school at that time to give guidance, and that all colleagues and students will work together to plan this major celebration. Now, please listen to Minister Sun's speech.

Minister Sun's Speech Distinguished Guests, Faculty, and Students, In the past two years, I have said at this school that Jiaotong University is a specialized school in China with a glorious history and long tradition. In the past fifteen years, many talents for national construction have been cultivated by this school, and they can be seen in government agencies and in society. This historical glory naturally makes us feel satisfied. However, the cultivation of talents by a school cannot be separated from the needs of the country and the spirit of society. As the needs of the country increase, our university must also develop day by day in order to achieve the original intention of establishing and maintaining Jiaotong University. Now, China has entered a period of peaceful construction, and the country's needs in the future will naturally be very large. At the same time, the revitalization of industry and commerce also urgently feels the need for talent. In this way, since the number of specialized talents needed by the country and society has increased, the strength of our school in cultivating specialized talents must also increase accordingly. The Ministry and the school, in view of this, decided on a plan to promote the development of the school. The first step is to engage in material construction. In the past two years, considerable achievements have been made. The construction of this Engineering Hall was actually planned by the school several years ago. President Ling also initiated it at that time, but because of financial difficulties, the government had no way to implement the construction. It is only now that there is hope of completion. Today is the groundbreaking ceremony. We hope that the entire building will be completed this year. After completion, it will not only be that Jiaotong University has increased its facilities, but it can be said that it has opened a new chapter in the national universities of the entire Chinese education community. The construction of the Engineering Hall has a great relationship with the development of our school. I hope that whether it is faculty or students, they will all strive to improve their knowledge and study practical sciences. What is studied today can be used to serve society tomorrow, to revitalize various industries, and to work together to promote it. It is not only the glory of our school, but also the happiness of the country and society. This is the opinion I contribute to the ceremony today.

Letter from the Consolidated Tax Department to the Yarn Mill Association 91

Tax Exemption for Inventory Until the End of March

Tax Reduction for Straw and Small Packages Not Approved

The Chinese Yarn Mill Association received a letter from the Consolidated Tax Department of the Ministry of Finance, which stated: Regarding the method of levying taxes on cotton yarn leaving the factory, your association previously submitted eight key points and sent representatives to petition the department. The department considered that the requests for extending the tax exemption period for inventory and reducing taxes on small and straw packages were important matters related to tax policy and could not be approved by the department without authorization. The situation was immediately reported to the Ministry of Finance for instructions. Now, instructions have been received that, with the implementation of the consolidated tax on cotton yarn, all inventory before February 1st will be allowed to be transported and sold within the prescribed time limit and will be exempt from tax, following the same tax collection method as machine-made foreign goods. This kind of accommodation already shows consideration for the difficulties of merchants. However, the first half of February coincides with the end of the lunar year, and transportation is stagnant, which is somewhat difficult in terms of commercial practice. Inspection and verification show that this is indeed the case. The transport and sale of inventory is temporarily allowed to be extended to March 31st. There will be no further extensions after this date. This is a special accommodation method at the beginning of the implementation. In the future, if there is a tax increase, all goods stored in the factory should still be implemented from the date of the tax increase, and this example should not be used as a precedent. As for the request to exempt the cotton on January 31st from consolidated tax, with 360 catties converted into one bale of yarn, it is difficult to implement and may affect other tax revenues, so it is impossible to approve. This time, the government abolished likin and implemented a new tax system, which has resulted in great losses, but it is all for the purpose of unifying the tax system and facilitating merchants. The manufacturers should be aware of the government's efforts to benefit merchants and eliminate malpractices, and should no longer worry excessively or make excessive demands. Regarding the request to reduce the consolidated tax on straw and small packages of cotton yarn, it should be known that the consolidated tax is a new tax system, and in principle, there can be no distinction between light and heavy. Moreover, since the tax rules have been determined and promulgated, the country's credibility, both internally and externally, is extremely important, and it is even more important not to change them rashly. It is hoped that you will inform your members to abide by the above and so on. Upon receiving this, we should comply with it. As for the other petitions regarding collection procedures, in order to strive to accommodate commercial situations, the department will be able to make accommodations if the method can be simplified without affecting tax revenue, in order to conform to the government's utmost concern for commerce. The department will also consider the various articles requested by your association in detail and decide on temporary measures with your association's representatives as follows: (1) The cotton yarn tax payment certificate will be temporarily stamped by the local consolidated tax bureau and issued to the factory representatives for the manufacturers to fill out and collect at any time. (2) The procedure for brushing and printing inspection numbers on the yarn bales is more complicated. It is temporarily allowed to be changed to stamping a mark with the three characters "徵統稅一" (consolidated tax one) made of coir on the yarn bale as proof of tax payment. (3) After the manufacturer applies for the tax payment certificate and stamps the "徵統稅一" (consolidated tax one) coir mark on the package surface, it can be shipped from the factory and sold locally. Those who transport and sell it elsewhere must report to the first-level management office or inspection office that it passes through (the location of the first-level management office or inspection office should be determined by each bureau and office based on the situation). After verifying that the goods and certificates match, the tax payment certificate will be stamped with a mark, and it can pass through without further inspection. (4) It is temporarily allowed for factories in Nantong, Wuxi, and Bizhou and other inland areas to ship in small packages as usual, and to accumulate forty small packages as one large package to pay the tax, without having to obtain a certificate. However, each factory must quickly establish a retail department. Once the retail department is established, no more zero packages can be shipped. (5) If the yarn mill has a weaving workshop, the cloth should be taxed first according to the yarn. From the first of this month, the amount of yarn sent by each factory to the weaving workshop should be reported for supplementary tax. Those who do not want to pay the tax on the yarn can report the brand name, number, weight, and other details of the woven cloth to the factory representative for verification and registration before shipping from the factory. Then, the grade will be determined, and the tax will be supplemented on the cloth. (6) The tax standard for each bale of cotton yarn is: for those below 23 counts, each large bale of 40 small packages is calculated as 312 catties; for those exceeding 20 counts, each large bale is calculated as 310 catties. The above temporary measures are extraordinarily accommodated by the department and will be submitted for approval. In addition to distributing them to the subordinate agencies to comply with, it should also be sent to your association to let all manufacturers abide by and implement them to enrich national taxes. This is most important.

The Various Industry Tax Rules Association Continues to Submit Opinions on Business Tax 92

Continued Submission to the Ministry of Finance

The Tax Rules Research Committee of the various industry trade associations in this city yesterday continued to submit to the Ministry of Finance, Nanjing National Government, "Regarding the audit and approval of the submitted document No. 11945 of the Junfu [Ministry of Finance], which was submitted to petition for the correction of the Zhejiang Province Business Tax Regulations and to conduct assessment and correction at any time to comply with the outline, and to pray for investigation and approval to relieve commercial difficulties and benefit commerce. We have reviewed and learned that the draft Business Tax Regulations of Zhejiang Province has been submitted to the ministry by the provincial government, and the ministry is in the process of reviewing each item. If the business classification, tax standards, and tax rates exceed the provisions of the ministerial outline and supplementary measures, they should be amended separately and then submitted to the provincial government for reply and transferred to the Finance Department for compliance. It is hoped that you will be informed of this decision." We have received this information, and we deeply appreciate the ministry's concern for the people's suffering and its willingness to listen to their voices. However, after investigating the business tax rates formulated by the provinces of Jiangsu and Zhejiang, there are many instances where they exceed the provisions of the outline and supplementary measures. We respectfully submit a brief explanation to the ministry for your kind consideration. (1) After investigating the general outline of business taxes in various provinces, except for luxury businesses and others that should be cracked down on, the maximum tax rate should not exceed 2/1000. However, the tax rates formulated by the provinces of Jiangsu and Zhejiang mostly exceed 2/1000, which is in obvious contradiction with the provisions of the outline. Moreover, the separate taxation of local and foreign goods is in violation of Article 7 of the supplementary measures. This is the first issue that we request the ministry to strictly correct. (2) Business tax should be levied on business operations, but the tax rates formulated by the provinces of Jiangsu and Zhejiang are based on items, which is a repeat of the mistake of the hundred-goods likin donation and opens the door to harassment by minor officials. Moreover, it is in contradiction with the naming of business tax. This is the second issue that we request the ministry to strictly correct. (3) The collection of business tax should be limited to those who engage in buying and selling activities. However, the so-called "zhuangke" (wholesale agents) in the market do not constitute buying and selling activities. For example, egg factories in Shanghai set up "zhuang" in the interior, only buying and not selling. Similarly, in the yarn and cloth industry, branches are set up in Haimen and Nantong to collect cloth, and another "zhuang" is established in Shanghai, but only for the convenience of handling and transportation. If these "zhuangke" also have to pay business tax, it is tantamount to a kind of buying and selling activity and paying double business tax. There are no explicit provisions for this in the business tax rates formulated by the provinces of Jiangsu and Zhejiang, and there will be many disputes during collection in the future. This is the third issue that we request the ministry to include in its consideration and exempt these "zhuangke" from business tax. The above reasons are entirely based on the submissions of various industries and integrated. We urge the ministry to consider the difficulties of merchants and, when revising the business tax in Jiangsu and Zhejiang, to ensure that all rates do not exceed 1/1000, except where the government has other regulations below 2/1000. The wholesale part should be taxed at 1/4, in accordance with the provisions of the outline. The collection method should be modeled after that formulated by the Anhui Provincial Government, and it should be handled in proportion to the turnover, so as to prevent harassment. In addition, "zhuangke" who do not engage in buying and selling activities should be exempt from business tax to avoid duplication. In this urgent telegram, we are filled with apprehension and await your instructions.

The Dyeing and Weaving Industry of Jiangsu and Zhejiang Requests Revision of the Business Tax Regulations 93

Telegram to the Ministry of Finance

The Dyeing and Weaving Industry of Jiangsu and Zhejiang telegraphed the Ministry of Finance yesterday, "To the Ministry of Finance of the National Government, We have investigated Article 4 of the Detailed Rules for the Consolidated Tax on Cotton Yarn issued by your ministry, which states that cotton yarn on which consolidated tax has already been paid and the cloth and other items directly woven from this cotton yarn are exempt from other types of national, provincial, or local taxes. Therefore, the business tax regulations of various provinces do not include the textile industry, because the cotton yarn and cloth produced by the textile industry have already been subject to consolidated tax. The dyeing and weaving manufacturing industry is a manufacturer of finished products woven from cotton yarn on which consolidated tax has been paid. The business nature of the dyeing and weaving industry is the same as that of textile factories, and it is of course exempt from all taxes and levies. Even the business tax regulations of various provinces list the cotton textile industry under the item of goods selling industry, and there are no provisions for further levying taxes on the cotton textile manufacturing industry. There is no need for further explanation. We humbly report this to your attention, and we respectfully request your ministry to issue an instruction to the finance departments of various provinces that when levying business tax on the dyeing and selling industry, the dyeing and weaving factories and their wholesale outlets (i.e., direct issuing offices) in the cotton textile manufacturing industry should not be involved. We also request your approval for strict compliance to benefit the industry."

Six Shipping Companies Operating Shanghai-Taiwan Liners Establish Escort Teams and Raise Fares 94

Three Guards Assigned to Each Ship First

To Be Implemented on the Second of This Month

Since the Xinning Taiwan liner was robbed and Taiwan bandits were discovered on the Guangji ship, navigation on the waters off Zhejiang has been very dangerous. The Lian'an Shipping Association in this city, because its six member companies' ships all travel to eastern Zhejiang, and because the Taiwan bandit Ye Mingsheng confessed during interrogation on the Chao Wu warship that he also planned to rob Shanghai-Taiwan liners, the six companies have now agreed to increase armed escorts to protect passengers. What we have heard is recorded below.

Request for Escort Teams The Lian'an Shipping Association's Daxi and Pingxing ships operate on the Shanghai-Taiwan line. The association has now decided to follow the example of the Sanbei, Ning Shao, and China Merchants Bureau ships operating on the Shanghai-Ningbo line and also request the placement of escort teams. The association has submitted a public request to the Songhu Garrison Headquarters to first dispatch 20 soldiers with pistols and wooden holsters to protect everything on the ship. The allowances will be provided by the Shipping Bureau. This has been approved, and the escort will be dispatched starting on the 18th and will be implemented starting on the 20th when departing. Three guards will be assigned to each ship first, and two or three more will be added in the second stage to strengthen the force.

Increase in Passenger Fares The six companies need to increase expenses for adding security guards. After a joint meeting of the Lian'an Shipping Association, it was decided that, starting from the opening of the classes on March 20th, the passenger cabin fares for ships from Shanghai to Haimen, Zhoushan, and other ports will be increased uniformly, about 20 percent more than the original fares. After the decision was made yesterday, it was announced to all sectors of society. As for freight rates, they are still under negotiation.

The Sino-French Radio Station Will Officially Communicate 95

The French Are Currently Transferring the Project

The Sino-German Electrical Equipment Has Also Been Completed

The International Radio Station established by the Ministry of Communications in Zhenru, except for the Sino-American portion that has officially communicated directly, the other Sino-French and Sino-German electrical equipment has not yet officially communicated due to unfinished projects. It is now learned that the Sino-French radio equipment of the International Radio Station was contracted by the French Long-Distance Telephone Company, and our country paid the project fee of more than 40,000 yuan. The installation started on March 11th last year and was completed in the first ten days of this month. Starting the day before yesterday (12th), the French Long-Distance Telephone Company, together with our country's radio engineers, is officially testing and communicating with Paris. It is planned to complete eight major tests. During the testing period, if any incorrect information is found in the communication, the French Long-Distance Telephone Company will still be responsible for repairing it. As for the incoming and outgoing telegrams, there is no degree of incorrectness. In order to complete its responsibilities, it will then be transferred to our country's Ministry of Communications for acceptance and communication. However, after our country accepts the project, it will still need to conduct local testing of the machine to understand the internal workings of the project. If any instability is found, the company will still be responsible for repairing it. The Sino-German electrical equipment project was installed by our country itself and was completed last month. Currently, it is communicating directly with Germany. On the German side, it has repeatedly requested to publicly and voluntarily test report for one day without charging telegram fees to gain the trust of all sectors of society. However, whether or not to hold a voluntary test report has not yet been decided by the Ministry of Communications.

Telegram Regarding the Disaster in Lingbao 100

Without Prompt Relief, They Will Turn Into Worms

The Chinese Red Cross Society received a telegram from Chairman Zhang Fang of the Henan Relief Committee, stating, "To the Chinese Red Cross Society, We have recently received a report from Zhang Lie, the magistrate of Lingbao County, and Dong Faxun, a disaster investigation committee member, stating that Lingbao has been hit by military disasters and banditry. Since last year, the Northwest Army has extorted military salaries, provisions, bran fodder, materials, grass, and opium, totaling more than 2.44 million yuan. More than 3,500 heads of livestock and more than 910 carts have been forcibly requisitioned, and the commutation price for conscription is more than 84,000 yuan. This year, bandits are rampant, and 5,600 houses have been burned down and more than 2,200 people have been kidnapped. Property worth approximately 1.1 million yuan has been looted, and 470 people have been murdered. The reduction in harvests due to drought and locusts and the deaths due to epidemics are not included. Now, as the severe winter approaches, they are suffering from both hunger and cold. Without prompt relief, they will turn into worms. Lingbao is a key point in Henan Province. Frequent military and bandit destruction has left the survivors unable to breathe. We earnestly request your organization to consider the survivors and provide grain and funds as soon as possible, and to widely publicize this to promote relief. We are most grateful. Zhang Fang of the Henan Relief Committee."

Six Companies Fined for Not Affixing Stamps to Invoices 103

Yesterday morning at 9:00 AM, the Special District Court heard a case initiated by the Public Works Department's lawyer regarding violations of the Stamp Tax Ordinance. The summoned parties included six businesses: Shujin Lane's Yonghexiang Company, Pentang Lane Bridge's Gu Rongxing Salt Store, Qipan Street's Qixin Bookstore, Guizhou Road's Changhe Rice Store, Fude Road's Yongfaxiang Fruit Store, and Sima Road's Huamei Pharmacy. Presiding over the trial was Magistrate Li Hongye. All were found guilty of not affixing stamps to invoices. The court immediately sentenced Yonghexiang, Qixin Bookstore, and Changhe Rice Store each to a fine of ten silver dollars. Gu Rongxing Salt Store and Yongfaxiang Fruit Store were each fined forty silver dollars. However, Huamei Pharmacy had been fined once before on September 10th of the previous year, making this a second offense, and thus the fine was increased to fifty silver dollars. Six other businesses, including Qinghe Inn, Ronghexiang, Zhiyuan Company, Senda Timber Company, and the nine major silk and satin stores including Hechun, were not present and their cases were rescheduled.

Local News Two

Silver Shanghai 107

Snow fell for twelve hours from the night before to yesterday afternoon.

The accumulated snow on the roads reached over a foot.

Since the beginning of spring, there has been continuous rain and snow. Yesterday's snow was particularly heavy. Starting the previous evening, the weather suddenly changed from drizzling rain to sleet. After 6:00 PM, it snowed in bursts, stopping briefly between each. When it snowed, the pellets were quite large, making a rustling sound against the tiles, not only causing suffering for those traveling but also disturbing people's sleep. Around midnight, the sleet turned to snow, with petals like plum blossoms and clumps like willow catkins dancing in the wind until it stopped yesterday afternoon. This lasted for twelve hours. The snow accumulated to a foot on rooftops, and supple branches and withered trees were all weighed down. The streets were like a powder shop made of jade, instantly turning Shanghai into a silver city. The following are noteworthy observations due to the heavy snow:

The Cleaners Overwhelmed: With so much accumulated snow everywhere, the cleaners were suddenly overwhelmed. Traffic in several places was blocked in the early morning. Although various vehicles did not stop even slightly in the prosperous areas, the snow turned to puddles after being rolled over by vehicle tires, causing suffering to pedestrians.

Rickshaw Drivers Profiteering: Rickshaw drivers took the opportunity to profiteer, increasing fares several times over the usual price. Coinciding with the end of the lunar year, when businesses were closing accounts, bill collectors lamented, "I can't go anywhere, brother!"

Streetcars Difficult to Operate: The weather in Shanghai has been very cold for several days. The day before yesterday, it rained heavily all day, and ice fell at times. The sound of ice pellets striking the roof tiles was like hail in summer. Last night, it snowed heavily all night until noon yesterday. The accumulated snow on the roads reached about a foot. This morning, all streetcars in both the Chinese and foreign concessions were suspended. They only started operating gradually by noon. At around 1:30 PM in the afternoon, the electric wires installed near Nanjing Road on Jing'an Temple Road in the Public Concession experienced a temporary shortage of current due to the heavy snow, causing streetcars on routes 1, 2, 3, 5, 6, and 7 to stop and be unable to move forward, resting along the way for about twenty minutes. Traffic only resumed after the current was sufficient.

Telephone Service Affected: More than twenty telephone lines on the section of Zhongxing Road in Zhabei Telephone Bureau, east of Taiyuan Fang, were broken by the accumulated snow, hanging down into the road like tangled hair. Unaware pedestrians avoided them, fearing electric shock. There were few residents and vast open spaces along the Shanghai-Minhang-Nanzhe Road, Luhuajing, and Xietu Road. Many telephone poles erected by the Telephone Bureau had already been broken by the heavy snow on the night of the 10th and had not yet been repaired, and the heavy snow on the night of the 13th caused most of the poles to suffer, with the telephone wires falling to the ground, making communication difficult. Furthermore, all telephones in Wusong and Baoshan were out of service yesterday. The Songyang Telephone Company issued a notice to users yesterday stating: "Dear Customers, Due to the continuous heavy snow, all lines have been damaged. Repairs are temporarily impossible to begin. We have no choice but to temporarily suspend telephone service. We hereby notify you."

Reduced Supply of Rice and Vegetables: The heavy snow did not stop, and rice boats were blocked, leading to a scarce supply in Shanghai. According to rice merchants, the market price has risen by several jiao per dan. At the same time, vegetable vendors braved the cold to come to Shanghai, and the prices of vegetables also increased several times. The poor are all complaining.

A Poor Man Freezes to Death: The weather was severely cold, with rain and snow covering the roads. The poor in Bietianyuan could not escape its onslaught. Therefore, a poor man in Pudong, about twenty years old, was lodging under the bridge of the old Xiangyan Factory, using the bridge's shelter as a natural stone house to avoid the wind and snow. However, lacking any means of warmth, he eventually froze to death. Yesterday, the court confirmed the death and arranged for the body to be collected.

Xue Die Contract Termination Case 108

This month on the 28th at 9:00 AM

To be heard by Magistrate Zhou Daren

Film actress Hu Die and Lin Xuehuai had previously made an engagement agreement, originally planning to marry after a considerable period. Unexpectedly, last winter, Lin suddenly sent a letter to Hu Die proposing to terminate the engagement, leading to a lawsuit. The case was initially filed in the Shanghai District Court but had not yet been opened for trial. Subsequently, Hu Die discovered that Lin Xuehuai resided at No. 171, near Beishanxi Road (Boundary Road) in the Public Concession. According to the law, the case should be heard in the Special District Court because the defendant resides there. To avoid jurisdictional disputes in the future, Hu Die's attorney, Zhan Jifeng, filed a petition with the Shanghai District Court to transfer jurisdiction. After investigating Lin's address and confirming that it was indeed in the concession, the court granted the request and transferred the case files to the Special District Court. However, a long time has passed, and there has been no date set for the opening of the trial, leading to the widely circulated Hu-Lin contract termination case appearing to have calmed down. Although the general public is paying close attention, there is no way to ascertain the truth. According to reliable information from the Special District Court, the case file regarding the Hu-Lin contract termination case was recently sent from the District Court to the Special District Court. The court has scheduled the case for trial in the ninth courtroom at 9:00 AM on the 28th of this month, to be presided over by Magistrate Zhou Daren. Hu Die's attorney will still be Zhan Jifeng, while Lin's representative attorney will be E Sen. It is expected that there will be a fierce debate when the trial opens.

Bloodshed in Heavy Snow 109

Cui Laoqi Murdered

Cui Laoqi, a Shandong native, thirty-seven years old, residing in Haigeli, Xuhui, was returning home from outside at 2:00 AM the night before last. At the time, it was snowing heavily, and there was no one walking on the road. Cui was ambushed and hacked to death with an axe on the road at Yangjiaku, Haige Road. He was wounded in the head and other places, and his entire body was covered in blood. The snow-covered ground was stained red. The murderer fled immediately, and no one knew anything about it. It was not discovered until yesterday morning, and the Second Precinct of the Sixth District ordered an investigation, considering two possibilities: revenge killing or robbery. Wang Mao, the head of the fifth tu of the twenty-eighth bao, was ordered to report the case to the District Court. Prosecutor Yang, along with coroner Xuan Zhiming and others, arrived at the scene to examine the body. It was ordered that the family prepare the coffin and await investigation.

Zhao Guangyu Died Tragically 110

Bloodstains Messily on the Pillow

Fingers Appeared Cyanotic

The night before last (the 13th) at 10:00 PM, a man claiming to be Zhao Guangyu from Shandong, about thirty years old, alone, checked into a room at a certain hotel at No. 245, Avenue Edward VII, in the French Concession. He was led to room 303 on the third floor by a receptionist. Zhao paid the room fee and immediately closed the door to sleep. It is unknown what caused him to suddenly become despondent and commit suicide by taking poison. At around 12:00 PM on the following afternoon, a waiter, Cao Wenqing, noticed that Zhao had not yet gotten up. According to the hotel's regulations, the time had expired, so he knocked on the room door to ask if the room needed to be extended. He only heard a vague response from inside, not specifying whether it was necessary or not. The waiter went to inquire in other rooms. Later, at around 2:00 PM, he still had not gotten up. He knocked on the door again to inquire but received no response. Suspecting something was wrong, he called other waiters to pry open the door and found that he had died. The cashier immediately reported it to the Grand Clock Tower Police Station, which sent detectives to investigate. The deceased was stout, of medium height with a round face, and had a Western-style haircut. The bedding next to the pillow was messily stained with blood, and his fingers were cyanotic. He was wearing a padded jacket of plain blue satin, a thin cotton vest of blue feather satin, a short shirt of white-bottomed blue-striped flannel, and a vermilion undershirt. He was wearing grey cloth padded trousers, blue crepe silk outer trousers, and white cotton socks with wrapped leggings. The quilt was covered with a dark grey sesame-thread woolen camel hair robe and a white-grey sesame-thread single jacket. Two letters addressed to Wu Daosheng were found in his pocket. The body was carried to the Tongren Fuyuan branch autopsy station. At the same time, detectives took the letters back to the police station to report to the detective chief, awaiting an autopsy and the detective, based on the address written on the letters, investigated the family.

Director Pan Discusses the Municipal Government's Policy on Handling the Riyue Case 111

Mayor Zhang has instructed the Social Affairs Bureau to supervise and liquidate the case at any time.

Four lawyers, Wu, Chen, Qin, and Jiang, have been entrusted to represent the creditors.

The liquidation of Riyue Bank and the Savings Department of the Great World is attracting social attention. The Wuchen Society reporter specially visited Director Pan of the Social Affairs Bureau yesterday to inquire about the Municipal Government's policy on handling this case. Director Pan gave a detailed explanation, which is recorded as follows: The Municipal Government has always paid attention to this case. Its sole purpose is to safeguard the interests of all creditors and to prevent any prejudice against poor depositors. Now that the judicial authorities have separately accepted the case, sent personnel to liquidate it, or seized property, and the creditor group has not expressed a consistent opinion, the Municipal Government is not in a position to take administrative action at the same time. I have been instructed by Mayor Zhang to instruct the Social Affairs Bureau to supervise the liquidation at any time, to prevent confusion or prejudice. Most of the creditors are women, laborers, and small depositors, and some may not be familiar with legal procedures, leading to the loss of rights. Therefore, the Bureau is responsible for providing guidance and has contacted four lawyers, Wu Jingxiong, Chen Xuerui, Qin Liankui, and Jiang Yiping, to ask them to act as representatives and participate in the litigation on behalf of more than ten thousand creditors. The four lawyers, with a sense of public service, have all generously agreed to fulfill their obligations. The Bureau will formally send letters of engagement tomorrow and publish a notice. If there are any creditors who have not yet registered, or those who have previously registered with accountant Xu Yongzuo but have not participated in the litigation, they can contact the offices of the four lawyers separately as soon as possible to be represented in court. As for the future liquidation results, if the assets of Gongfa Company are insufficient to cover its debts, the directors and shareholders should be jointly responsible. The list of shareholders is being secretly investigated.

Petition by Vegetable Vendors on Ximen Road in the French Concession 115

The vegetable vendors in the middle section of Ximen Road in the French Concession have been setting up stalls and operating their businesses after donating for licenses at the Grand Clock Tower Public Works Department. However, since December of last year, the French Public Works Bureau, at the request of the Nanyang Bridge Business Association, stopped issuing licenses, claiming that they obstructed pedestrian traffic. This directly affected these vegetable vendors who relied on setting up stalls, totaling more than ninety households, resulting in unemployment and making it impossible for more than a thousand people to make a living. Although they still resumed operating covertly at the beginning and end of the alley, they were frequently subjected to detention and fines. Furthermore, during the period of lunar new year account settlement, which is usually a time of thriving business, they had no choice but to seek unity and make a final appeal. A few days ago, they elected representatives Yan Wenguang, Wang Shangyi, Zhao Jinkun, Lu Peiqing, Zhi Jinneng, Li Dagen, Wang Ayu, and others to petition the Chinese Taxpayers Association of the French Concession, the French Public Works Department Donation Office, the Municipal Party Headquarters, and the Social Affairs Bureau, and to sincerely request Mr. Du, Chairman of Huagene Road, to consider the livelihoods of the common people, speak up for justice, and find ways to help. Mr. Du's residence sent Mr. Yang to meet with them on his behalf, promising to find a way, or to designate other straight roads such as Ma Lang Road and Jule Road for business operations, so that there would be no obstruction to the road administration. Each representative was satisfied and dispersed. However, the end of lunar new year account settlement period has arrived, and it is uncertain whether licenses can be obtained in these one or two days. These more than ninety households and over a thousand poor people are still frowning with suffering.

Silk and Satin Dyeing Industry Temporarily Does Not Increase Prices 117

Abiding by the Agreed Price List Preserves Credibility

The Shanghai Silk and Satin Dyeing Industry Association sent a letter to various silk shops regarding the settlement of the final dyeing accounts for the year 19, stating: "Greetings. Due to the soaring price of gold, independent tariffs, and rising raw material costs, the operating costs are enormous. Various industries have increased prices to seek compensation. The main raw material used by our industry, dyes, has risen to three or four tenths, making it difficult to maintain operations. We could have increased dyeing fees appropriately to remedy this. However, in February of the year 19, before your industry sent items for dyeing and before our industry received items for dyeing, there were agreed price lists stamped, stipulating the prices of various colors. Increasing prices midway would inevitably harm our credibility. Furthermore, according to our industry, there were still violations of the agreed price list and deductions of dyeing fees during the first and second periods of the year 19 settlement of dyeing accounts. If there is no increase in price and further deductions are made this time during the final period of the dyeing accounts, then the operations of each dyehouse in our industry will naturally not be able to be maintained. Our association's representatives have decided that all final dyeing accounts for the year 19 will be settled according to the prices stipulated in the agreed price list stamped with each silk shop in February of last year, temporarily enduring the pain and not increasing prices, to show our adherence to credibility. We should record this accordingly and respectfully inform you. We hope that your shop will adhere to the principle of good faith and commercial integrity, so that our industry's dyehouses will settle the final dyeing accounts for the year 19 with your shop according to the prices stipulated in the previous agreed price list, without further deductions or delays. We would be publicly grateful."

Guangdong Boy Scouts National Hiking Team Arrives in Shanghai 118

Will Transfer to Sichuan, Kangding, Yunnan and Other Places to Investigate

Guangdong Boy Scout Comrade Deng Jinhui, set off from Guangdong in the first month of the eighteenth year of the Republic of China to hike across the country, and has now been more than two years. Qidong Sends a Ship to Fetch Wanted Criminals 121

The Shanghai County Public Security Bureau recently learned that a gang of bandits who had repeatedly committed murder, arson, robbery, intimidation, and fraud in Qidong County were hiding in No. 12 Hongyunfang in the French Concession. It sent a full squad of detectives, together with the French police, to rush to the house and arrest seven people, including Wang Chunfu, Zhu Hanping, Yu Er, and Lu Guangren. At the same time, a formal document was being prepared to request the Qidong County Government to transfer the suspects for interrogation. Therefore, County Magistrate Zhou Juesheng personally led the Chief Prosecutor Su Zihu and others, taking the county's warship to Shanghai. The County Government requested to fetch and take them back. By order of the County Government, the Public Security Bureau yesterday extracted the four suspects, Wang et al., from the detention center, handed them over to the county's Team Leader Su and others, escorted them onto the warship, and took them back to Qidong for trial.

Two Young Girls Suddenly Arrive at a Pancake Shop 122

Wang Xia Shi, a woman from Bao Ying, forty-one years old, residing next to the Taitong Inn on North Hutang Road, Pudong, runs a pancake shop at home to make a living. New Wireless Radio 123

Can Make Your Own Records

Among the new wireless radio receiving sets, there is one that can create its own records. The method is extremely simple and the application is very broad. According to Mr. Diley, General Manager of Wheeler Company, the new receiver is equipped with a nine-sound return line, the volume can be adjusted at will when receiving sounds, and the sound quality is clear. Its internal structure is unusually simple, the model is the same as ordinary large wireless radios. When using, just turn on the machine knob, the sound wave is accurate, and you can print distant and near pleasant music, singing and dancing or personal talks, one by one, without any drawbacks. The disc is double-sided, and can be taken out and played immediately.

The body of the No. 80 wireless radio is low, made of five layers of walnut wood shell. The No. 82 has a cylindrical shell, carved double doors, and a tuner. The No. 86 is a home-made record player, also a walnut wood shell with engraved copper knobs and double doors. The four-use switch of the instrument can receive and transmit radio and record discs, which is indeed a new era in the wireless radio industry.

Robbers Brave the Snow to Commit Robbery 124

Five Arrested by Police Following Snow Tracks

Wu A Yuan's family, a local resident living at No. 27 near the Yunzao River in Wusong, was suddenly visited by five or six robbers at around 12:00 PM the night before last, while it was snowing heavily. Page 12

Rumors are rife that the anti-opium authorities are preparing for a public sale of opium, causing widespread anxiety. People from all walks of life are running around spreading the news, and telegrams and letters are flying. The reason for this is said to be well-founded. The Customs has allegedly been entrusted by the authorities to draft the regulations for the public sale. Ji Hong, who claims to be an expert in handling opium taxes, has also, under the order of the Ministry of Finance, led Guanwu Shuyao Yao and Zhou Zhizhen to Taiwan to investigate the local opium public sale methods, intending to imitate them. The local overseas Chinese are extremely shocked and have sent urgent telegrams to this association to lodge a serious protest. At the same time, Wu Liande, who is close to the anti-opium authorities, has publicly advocated for the implementation of opium public sale in the newspapers and has published this article as a separate pamphlet, distributing it both domestically and abroad. Wu Liande, as a member of this association, has made such remarks, which not only violate the overall position of this association but also contradict his own consistent stance. Everyone has their own aspirations, and it is understandable that opinions cannot be forcibly aligned. However, this association should solemnly declare that it absolutely does not sympathize with Wu's personal opinions. Recently, Li Jihong, who went to Taiwan to investigate the public sale, and Wu Liande, who openly advocates for public sale, have both been formally appointed as members of the Anti-Opium Committee. Furthermore, Liu Ruiheng, the chairman of the committee, did not explicitly deny the public sale in his conversation with the Daily News reporter, as reported in the Shishi Xinbao on February 13th. This indicates that the anti-opium authorities' policy of adopting public sale is already in full swing and is by no means unfounded. The colleagues of this association, adhering to the late Dr. Sun Yat-sen's instructions and the people's entrustment, are engaged in the anti-drug movement, hoping to promote the implementation of opium prohibition. Regarding the policy of opium public sale, we have conducted many years of research and investigations in various countries. Based on our experience and findings, we deeply know that it has a hundred disadvantages and not a single advantage. Therefore, we have passed a resolution in the regular meeting to express our firm opposition. We will use our fearless spirit to protest against public sale. Now, I will present my humble opinions in the following points for the consideration of the nation: (1) Opium public sale is a total bankruptcy of political morality. Opium is a poisonous substance that can destroy a nation and extinguish its people. Public sale is an aggressive policy imposed by the great powers on their colonies. Therefore, they absolutely prohibit their own citizens from smoking, and offenders are punished with ten years of imprisonment. However, they allow our overseas Chinese to indulge in it. Their premeditation can be seen. If it is implemented in our own country, what is the difference between suicide and murder? To allow people to smoke poisonous substances through law as a way to raise funds is truly unprecedented and unheard of at home and abroad. If it is implemented, it will lead to a total bankruptcy of our country's political morality and will be abandoned by the people of the whole country. Anyone with a conscience should not consider raising funds by poisoning the people as feasible. This is the first reason why opium public sale is unacceptable. (2) Opium public sale violates international faith. Since the British smuggled opium into our country, people from all walks of life have been deeply saddened by the opium disaster and have worked hard to resist it. The pioneering figure in opium prohibition, Tang Shaoyi, first initiated and signed the Sino-British Opium Prohibition Treaty. Later, various countries signed the Hague Opium Convention, which was also signed by our country, to strictly prohibit opium within the country. Subsequently, at various international conferences, our representatives, based on the public opinion of the government and the people, opposed the great powers' implementation of opium public sale policies in their colonies and made every effort to attack and demand its cancellation. Recently, the Ministry of Foreign Affairs issued an opium prohibition declaration on January 9th, also clearly protesting. At the international anti-opium conference on opium public sale, our representative Wu Kaisheng followed the declaration and protested at the conference. Looking at our country's words and actions towards foreign countries before and after, we have always opposed public sale. If we now take it upon ourselves, our international status will be completely lost, and our national credibility will be destroyed from then on. Thinking of this, I cannot help but shudder. This is the second reason why opium public sale is unacceptable. (3) Opium public sale violates the late Dr. Sun Yat-sen's instructions. Throughout his life, Dr. Sun Yat-sen deeply hated and detested opium. In 1924, he issued an anti-drug statement, clearly stating that opium business can never coexist with the national government empowered by the people. He also said that anyone who advocates for legalizing the opium business and allowing customs to permit opium imports in order to enrich revenue is a public enemy of the people, even as a temporary expedient. If a responsible government agency allows opium to exist for its own convenience and does not care about the long-term consequences, it is an act of treason. Dr. Sun Yat-sen created the Republic, and his instructions should be followed by future generations and should not be violated. Anyone who advocates for opium public sale is violating his anti-drug instructions. This is the third reason why opium public sale is unacceptable. (4) Opium public sale violates the party platform and the law. The Kuomintang platform clearly stipulates the prohibition of opium traffic. The laws of the National Government also advocate for the complete prohibition of opium traffic. Repeatedly and repeatedly, explicit orders have been promulgated. In November of the 17th year of the Republic (1928), the central government held a national anti-opium conference, which passed 44 resolutions to completely prohibit opium. Government dignitaries and parliamentary speeches also unanimously advocated for complete prohibition and not using opium as a source of tax revenue. The representatives attending the conference, from ministers of the National Government and various departments to representatives of various countries, all swore to Dr. Sun Yat-sen to prohibit opium. All of these facts are known at home and abroad. If we now abandon the policy of prohibition and implement public sale, where will we place the Kuomintang platform, the anti-opium laws, and the first national anti-opium conference? Anti-opium laws are not child's play and cannot be changed overnight. This is the fourth reason why opium public sale is unacceptable. (5) Opium public sale will make opium prohibition worse. Proponents of opium public sale often criticize the failure of the current anti-opium laws. However, they do not know that the reason why the current anti-opium laws cannot be implemented is not the fault of the laws but the government's failure to enforce them. The authorities have not been strict in enforcing the current anti-opium laws. In cases of large officials transporting opium, smoking opium, and soldiers planting opium and providing protection, even with conclusive evidence, they have not been punished according to the law. As a result, soldiers transporting opium has become an open secret. Those in high positions and with high salaries are often criminals who violate the anti-opium laws and even take pride in violating the laws and use opium business as a source of wealth. How can we expect the people to abide by the law? It is like climbing a tree to catch fish. The public destruction of the anti-opium laws by the special opium tax in Hubei and Hunan still wants to blame the current anti-opium laws for not being able to be implemented, which is truly incomprehensible. Therefore, the urgent task today is to respect the current anti-opium laws, give full play to their spirit, and promote their implementation with strength. We should first punish the big officials who violate the law in order to influence the people of the whole country. If we abandon the anti-opium laws and adopt a public sale policy, the people will be even more disappointed, and opium prohibition will only get worse. This is the fifth reason why opium public sale is unacceptable. (6) Opium public sale is a regression of politics. Although the poison of opium is deep, the authorities in the late Qing Dynasty, recognizing the suffering of the people and the major trends of the world, were still able to sign a ten-year opium prohibition treaty with the British and implement it vigorously. Anyone who violated the law, regardless of their position, would be punished to achieve prohibition, which was praised by the world. In the early years of the Republic of China, opium prohibition was strict. When Xu Shichang was president, he did not hesitate to spend 35 million yuan to buy the British opium and burn it to show his determination. Now, the revolutionary government, at a time when the internal strife has been settled and the period of political tutelage is beginning, is proposing opium public sale. This is tantamount to admitting that what the Qing Dynasty could do and what the Beiyang government could do, our National Government is powerless to do. We deeply advocate that opium has already been prohibited once. If the government is determined, it is not impossible to prohibit it again. If we do not exert our will and instead adopt a plan to raise funds through public sale, it is nothing short of promoting the regression of politics. This is the sixth reason why opium public sale is unacceptable. (7) Opium public sale will repeat the mistakes of state-run opium. Opium public sale has been implemented in our country many times, but all have failed. The most recent example is the opium public sale implemented by the Ministry of Finance in Jiangsu and Zhejiang in 1927 and 1928, which was full of ugly scenes and numerous malpractices. It was called raising funds for the government, but in reality, the government's revenue was less than a quarter of the budget, while the sales of opium were ten times higher than in the era of private trafficking. The shady secrets can be imagined. At that time, due to the strong opposition from the people, the National Government sent Councilor Zeng Boxingshi to Shanghai to investigate. His report to the central government strongly stated that the malpractices of state-run opium trafficking were numerous. Seeing that this method was not feasible, the National Government ordered its cancellation. If we now want to implement opium public sale, we are bound to repeat the mistakes of the past. The result will ultimately be more harm than good. This is the seventh reason why opium public sale is unacceptable. (8) Opium public sale will make the political situation even more chaotic. Now, those who advocate for opium public sale often complain that the military in various provinces privately collect opium taxes, amounting to tens of millions of taels, enriching themselves without benefiting the national treasury. However, they do not know that the central government's opium prohibition and the military in various provinces are still somewhat restrained. Once public sale is implemented, the military and officials will have an excuse to openly and brazenly levy taxes and enrich themselves. They will not necessarily turn over the opium taxes to the government due to the central government's public sale. If the central government has the ability to make them turn over all the opium taxes to the government, it would be better to use this ability to prohibit opium. The ancients said, "When those above and those below compete for profit, the country is in danger." Therefore, if public sale is implemented today, it will inevitably enable the military in various provinces to open up financial resources and consolidate their positions. The result will only make the situation even more chaotic and unmanageable. This is the eighth reason why opium public sale is unacceptable. (9) Opium public sale will inevitably lead to its indefinite cancellation. Opium public sale is a source of wealth for raising funds. The colonies of various countries rely on it as the largest source of revenue for government expenses. Therefore, although our country has protested many times over the past ten years, it has been impossible to cancel it. This is because once the revenue is so large, it is impossible to give it up. The Ministry of Finance previously established a tax office in Hankou, which was nominally temporary, but has been repeatedly extended and is unwilling to cancel it because the profits are high and they are reluctant to give it up. Our country's salt tax was also a temporary expedient, but it has only recently been cancelled, which shows the endless harm caused by the initial creation. Opium public sale may be advocated for ten or fifteen years, with annual revenue of over 100 million yuan. In the future, it will be impossible to cancel it within a fixed period. Advocating for government public sale is like leading a tiger to taste human blood, which will inevitably lead to the inability to stop it. This is the ninth reason why opium public sale is unacceptable. (10) Opium public sale will inevitably increase the number of opium addicts. Since opium public sale aims to raise funds, those who handle it will do everything possible to expand its sales to increase revenue. As a result, the number of opium addicts will inevitably increase, and the opium disaster will become more severe. The previous lessons of the British and Dutch possessions in Southeast Asia can serve as a warning. In the Straits Settlements and the Malay Peninsula, Chinese opium addicts account for more than 20% of the total population. It is undeniable that opium prohibition in our country has been lax. However, the number of smokers, in proportion, is only a quarter of that in British possessions. This situation can serve as a clear warning. This is the tenth reason why opium public sale is unacceptable. In short, opium public sale has a hundred disadvantages and not a single advantage. The country's economic difficulties should be solved in a fundamental way. It is absolutely impossible to quench thirst with poison, which will lead to endless disasters. I hereby declare my views and hope that the people of the country will respond in unison. The country will be fortunate, and the nation will be fortunate.

Wu Liande's Talk, reported by the Guowen News Agency: Mr. Wu Liande Fu Shi recently expressed his views on opium prohibition in his personal capacity, providing people with a common matter for research and consideration, which has aroused special attention from all parties. Reporters think that the issue of opium prohibition is something of concern to the whole country, and the opinions made by Dr. Wu Fu Shi are something readers would like to hear. Yesterday, the reporter visited Dr. Wu at the Jiu Jiang Za Hao office. The following is a record of the conversation:

I (Wu self-proclaimed) The article "The Opium Problem of Extreme Toxicity" published earlier was purely a personal observation of China for decades. "The toxicity of opium has reached its extreme, and today it has spread all over the world. Therefore, the opium problem is not a simple or local problem, but a problem of narcotics that the whole world should pay close attention to. It is not to say that China suffers the most. I am Chinese, and I have studied medicine all my life. In addition to seeking the happiness of mankind in the world, my love for my country has never gone away. Therefore, I have served the country for nearly 20 years. My words and deeds should also be well known to the people of the country. As for the object of opium, I am deeply saddened and disgusted. I believe that it is the greatest harm to mankind and a huge enemy of the Chinese nation. Since the signing of the Hague Convention, 20 years have passed. People talk about opium prohibition every day, but the atmosphere of opium is getting stronger. People talk about rejecting drugs, but the poison is spreading throughout the country. Overseas morphine factories are stepping up their efforts to produce and ship narcotic drugs to China in increasing quantities. We only hear the voice of the people rejecting drugs, but we have not seen any fundamental measures to reject drugs. Even palliative measures such as smoking cessation hospitals to give smokers a chance to quit smoking have not yet been established. Liande belongs to the people of the country, who are heartbroken by what they see, so he collected decades of experience and consulted the situation at home and abroad, considered it carefully, and published an article regardless of its shortcomings. It is not a tribute to the authorities, nor does it represent the views of any organization or group, nor is it a crazy person with ulterior motives, but a personal opinion in a question that everyone should study. The purpose is to completely ban opium and enable the Chinese nation to have a day to carry forward and magnify the light. I deeply hope that the people of the country will no longer just observe the opium problem with endless harm in a straight line and conduct in-depth research on it. Perhaps one idea in thousands of thoughts can be discussed by everyone. I especially hope that the press will give a careful identification and discussion to provide reference for the opium authorities and wake up the Chinese people's opium dream.

Establishment of the Chinese Branch of the International Chamber of Commerce 126

Organized by National Industrial Groups

The International Chamber of Commerce is a joint organization of chambers of commerce from 47 countries, including the United Kingdom, the United States, Germany, and France. It holds a very important position in international trade. At the first representative conference held by the Chamber in Paris, France, a few years ago, although Zhang Gongquan, Chen Guangfu, and others attended, they had not officially joined the Chamber. A few months ago, at a meeting of the China International Trade Association, Mr. Lin Kanghou of the banking community strongly stated the relationship between the International Chamber of Commerce and the future of international trade in our country at the meeting and advocated joining the Chamber in time to obtain international commercial status. The listeners were moved, so on the 7th of this month, various national industrial groups initiated the organization of the Chinese branch of the International Chamber of Commerce in Shanghai, and elected Chen Guangfu as the chairman, Guo Bingwen as the vice chairman, and Lin Kanghou as the secretary-general, and on the 13th, they sent a telegram to the Chamber in Paris, expressing their official accession.

Zhu Yan's Lecture on Land Issues 128

The City Has a Total Area of Over 1.27 Million Mu

Divided into Seventeen Districts, Using Qiu as the Unit

Zhu Yan, director of the Shanghai Land Bureau, gave a lecture at the Shanghai Municipal Research Association in the Sichuan Road Youth Association yesterday afternoon, titled "An Overview of Land Administration in Shanghai," with over 300 people in attendance. The lecture is recorded below as follows.

A few days ago, I heard that the gentlemen of the Municipal Research Association here are enthusiastic about studying various issues of municipal administration in this city and have invited colleagues from the municipal authorities to give lectures here. I am very happy about this. I have been invited to give a lecture on land administration in this city. However, the content of the item is very dry, but in order to clarify the progress of municipal administration in this city, I will give a brief report on this issue. In the past, there was no such name as land issues, so it can be called a new issue. The organization of the urban area is entirely based on the city organization law and the model of the Songhu Military Governor's Office. There are places such as Shangbao and Zhoupu, or because the boundaries of several counties intersect, the boundaries are unclear. After joint discussions by the central, provincial, and municipal governments, they have all been incorporated into the administrative area of the city. In the past, Shanghai was called a certain village or a certain city, etc. Now, these names have been uniformly abolished and changed to districts. After the reorganization, the city is divided into 17 districts. The concession area is called a special district. According to statistics, the city has an area of 1,272,000 mu, of which 731,000 mu have been taken over. The public concession area has 33,503 mu, and the French concession has 21,409 mu. However, the French concession also has a so-called new French concession area, which has 13,001 mu. The name of the new French concession area is not formally leased. It is actually due to Yuan Shikai's妄想妄想稱帝称帝 in the third year of the Republic (1914). In order to obtain the recognition of various countries, an agreement was signed with the French concession to allow the right to build roads beyond the boundary. The name at the time of signing was the road area outside the concession, and its area was several times larger than the original leased area. I hope that you will pay special attention to this issue. If you want to send letters in that area, you should call it a certain place and not treat it as a concession. Even the rest of the concessions should be called a certain concession and the word "concession" should not be omitted, so as not to be ridiculed by foreigners. The small parts of the original area were previously divided into Bao Tu and Wei Hao. In Baoshan County, there was one more Qiu name. After the Land Bureau took over, it was changed to Qu Tu Wei Hao Qiu, with Qiu as the unit to avoid the unevenness of the past. Before the establishment of the Land Bureau, land administration belonged to the county magistrate, and the county magistrate could only maintain the status quo on this issue and could not have innovative methods to improve it. Even the Qingzhang Bureau (land survey bureau) run by the local gentry had no evidence and could not have improved methods to remedy it. Moreover, there were many inconsistencies in the area of the region, and its funding could only be subsidized by adding eight points to the land tax. With insufficient economy and lack of talent, its inability to achieve good results was also an inevitable fact. Therefore, after the establishment of the Land Bureau, the first task was to take over the entire Qingzhang Bureau as the basis, and on the other hand, to take over the Land Register Office and the survey Bureau of the Baoshan Hall. Now the Land Bureau has professional talents and more scientific methods, which will surely lead to a good result. The first section of the four sections is divided into five units: (1) Document Unit (2) Accounting Unit (3) Cashier Unit (4) Collection Unit (5) General Affairs Unit. The second section is divided into four units: (1) Foreign Affairs Unit (2) Public Land Unit (3) Land Price Unit (4) Requisition Unit. The third section is divided into three units: (1) Unit (2) Unit (3) Kaogong Unit. The fourth section is (1) Registration Unit (2) Review Unit (3) Single Contract Unit. A writing office is also set up outside the bureau to facilitate the writing of petitions for the people.

Provincial Order to Protect Commercial Guilds 130

County Government Receives Provincial Order and Ministry Order

The Shanghai County Government yesterday received an instruction from the Jiangsu Provincial Government, which stated, "In order to comply with the matter, the Ministry of Industry has issued a notice stating that commercial guilds in various provinces and cities have traditionally been jointly operated by local merchants or those in the same trade, with the good intention of fostering relationships and developing commerce. Recently, merchant groups in various places have reported that their guild halls are often being occupied, confiscated, or their assets sold off. If this is indeed the case, it is highly inappropriate and contrary to the duties of the Ministry. The Ministry is currently seeking to consolidate the strength of merchants, implement unity, and collectively strive to deal with the outside world. Such historical organizations should be maintained and not recklessly destroyed. In addition to issuing separate orders, a corresponding order is hereby issued, instructing the county magistrate to investigate, strictly protect, and ensure commercial stability. This order is issued."

Resolution of Labor Dispute at Huayang Textile Factory 131

Each Worker to Receive 65 Yuan in Compensation from the Employer

The Huayang Textile Factory on Sanggongtang Road in the Shanghai South area, recognizing that the output of foot-pedal looms was low, began to convert to motorized machines in January. As a result, twenty male workers operating foot-pedal machines, including Shi Xiebong, were laid off, leading to a labor dispute. It is reported that the dispute was resolved on February 12 through negotiations between labor and management. As a result, the employer will provide each worker with a subsidy of 65 yuan, totaling 1,430 yuan, and terminate the employment relationship.

Reasons for Increased Chinese Language Instruction in Japanese Schools 132

Used as a Tool for Aggression Against Our Country

Tokyo Correspondence: Due to the impact of the economic downturn, Japan's unemployment rate has reached 400,000. Last year, only 30% of university and vocational school graduates found employment, creating a difficult job market. To open up new avenues for employment and reduce the number of unemployed, Japan is encouraging emigration to Manchuria. This spring, there will be over 20,000 graduates. A survey by the Bureau of Education regarding the future career aspirations of these students revealed that nearly half desired to go to Manchuria. However, they are hindered by their lack of proficiency in Chinese. Therefore, the Ministry of Education has mandated Chinese language as a compulsory subject in all levels of schools. The stated reason is the close relationship between Chinese and Japanese culture, and the need for Japan to emphasize Chinese language. In reality, this is to train language tools for aggression against our country. Chinese language is also taught in military schools and among soldiers, further revealing Japan's ambition towards our country.

Jiangsu Exam for Bureau of Education Directors Sent to the Examination Yuan for Review 133

Due to the lack of local educational administrative personnel, the former Central University's Administrative Yuan held two sessions of examinations for Bureau of Education directors, the first of their kind in the country for educational administrative personnel. The examination procedures and subjects were consistent with those promulgated by the current Examination Yuan. At the time, experts such as Meng Xiancheng, Cheng Shiyingui, Zheng Zonghai, Zhu Jingnong, Qin Fen, and Yu Qingtang were specially appointed to grade the papers, with strict criteria for selection. In the first session, Jin Yingyuan, Wang Lansheng, and Li Cheng were selected; in the second session, Jiang Yuanmin, Cao Zhongquan, Yao Renshou, Xie Zhimou, Chen Jing, Xie Wenle, Shao Guixiang, Feng Zanyuan, Gong Xuanxiao, Zhang Xichang, Lu Renshou, Ji Chengshu, Zheng Feiqing, Jia Shufa, Dong Guozhao, Gu Yanqing and others totaling sixteen people, were selected. They were subsequently appointed as directors of county education bureaus. Now, the Review Committee of the Central Examination Yuan has notified the provinces to submit the names for review within a specified period. The Jiangsu Department of Education has already submitted the list of directors who passed the two sessions of examinations, along with their resumes and documents, to the provincial government for forwarding to the Central Government for review.
